  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0afebd49-81f8-4327-a218-525bc04eb9f1'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer11741630746711895927">Oh Mia... As I mentioned in my last review.. it's during this stage that I have to give these books 4 stages instead of 5 because of how annoying Mia can get. She's only 15.. I get it. It's just a bit harder to read now that I'm older. Still really enjoyed it and it definitely made me laugh! Really wanting to speed through rereading the rest so I can read A Royal Wedding when it comes out!!</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12902719881506289714">Until the last few pages of the book, I was going to give this one star for the simple reason that I just did not like it. At all.<br/><br/>Some of my complaints (this is by no means a complete list):<br/><br/>*I need the adults in Mia's life to step up and start acting like the adults. When Mia came to her mother and was asking questions about sex, her mother probably should have pushed more and given Mia more information. It was CLEAR TO ME that Mia was not handling things well. I just really think Mia's mother s</span>
  <span id="freeText12902719881506289714" style="display:none">Until the last few pages of the book, I was going to give this one star for the simple reason that I just did not like it. At all.<br /><br />Some of my complaints (this is by no means a complete list):<br /><br />*I need the adults in Mia's life to step up and start acting like the adults. When Mia came to her mother and was asking questions about sex, her mother probably should have pushed more and given Mia more information. It was CLEAR TO ME that Mia was not handling things well. I just really think Mia's mother should have talked to Mia more.<br /><br />*Just in general, I was uncomfortable with the way sex was handled in this up until the conversation Mia and Michael had at the end of the book.<br /><br />*Mia vs. Lana for student council president? REALLY? They are sophomores. There are NO juniors or seniors who wanted to run?? This would have been a lot more believable if they had been running for sophomore class president.<br /><br />*I was all ready to like this book a little more during Mia's speech. The first part of it, that is. THEN SHE WENT OFF ON THAT TANGENT ABOUT HOW IT WAS OKAY FOR PEOPLE TO WRITE ABOUT BRITNEY SPEARS FOR ENGLISH. Well, no. Actually Mia, sometimes when your teacher tells you the assignment is to write about more serious subjects, you just do it. Sending your father to complain about your B? That's not okay, and I didn't like that this book made it seem like it WAS okay. I agree with your teacher, who is NOT being unreasonable. All I see Mia writing about are frivilous things, with a true teenage girl flair.<br /><br />*Honestly, I do not like any character in this book except Michael. And even he is sometimes confusing because I do not understand Michael/Mia. I need to be able to ship this but it is not working for me.<br /><br /><br /><br />The things I did like:<br /><br />*Principal Gupta is a fairly accurate portrayal of my experience with school authority, catering to Lana's complaints and ignoring how Lana is actually at the root of a lot of the problems. Honestly, Principal Gupta was probably more with it than a lot of the teachers/administrators in my experience. So, I guess this isn't something I "liked" so much as I found it fairly true to life. For the school experiences in this book, at least.<br /><br />*The New York stuff, as always, was excellent.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_740277061" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/740277061" />
    <a title="Adri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7391803-adri"><img alt="Adri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605327285p2/7391803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/740277061?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adri" href="/user/show/7391803-adri">Adri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061543654" href="/book/show/2068673.Princess_in_Training">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7391803-adri?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7391803-adri?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer740277061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14449030653775592435">In case you were not aware, I LOVE <i>The Princess Diaries</i> series. I have read all ten books (approximately) a million times, and they are so near and dear to my heart. This series played a huge role in my life (and my sister’s life) as I grew up, and I’m just having a blast rereading them this year.<br/><br/><i>Princess in Training</i> is actually one of my favorite books in the series—which, yes, I know it’s so meta to have favorite books in one of your favorite series.<br/><br/>In this installment, Mia is dealing with a l</span>
  <span id="freeText14449030653775592435" style="display:none">In case you were not aware, I LOVE <i>The Princess Diaries</i> series. I have read all ten books (approximately) a million times, and they are so near and dear to my heart. This series played a huge role in my life (and my sister’s life) as I grew up, and I’m just having a blast rereading them this year.<br /><br /><i>Princess in Training</i> is actually one of my favorite books in the series—which, yes, I know it’s so meta to have favorite books in one of your favorite series.<br /><br />In this installment, Mia is dealing with a lot of big things: on top of being a princess—and having to endure painful princess lessons with her Grandmère—she has to deal with her best friend, Lilly, nominating her for class president against Lana Weinberger; her boyfriend possibly wanting to deflower her; being a “baby-licker” and constantly worrying about her new-born brother and all the ways he can a) get sick, b) get hurt, and c) die; her ex-boyfriend constantly chatting her ear off about his new “perfect” girlfriend, Heather; and an English teacher who—gasp!—questions and criticizes her identity as a writer. Oh, and I forgot that the UN was trying to exile Genovia because of this whole “snail” situation—long story.<br /><br />As usual, there’s a lot going on in this novel and it’s crazy and out of control, but it’s so wonderful for the very same reasons. Mia is always so frantic and panicked—as she should be, did you even read the list above?—but she’s always hilarious and witty; her type of crazy just works for me. Every book in this series is always so enjoyable to read because of Mia’s sarcasm and her immaturity; she over-thinks EVERYTHING and has very little experience (like, in everything) but that’s kind of what makes her such an uproarious character/voice to read!<blockquote>
  <i>Everyone seems to think that Doing It is just, like, the pinnacle of experiences. Everyone except for me. Why am I the only person who, when she thinks about Doing It, feels nothing but…sweaty? And not in a good way. This can’t be a normal reaction. This has to be yet another genetic anomaly in my makeup, like absence of mammary glands and size-ten feet. I am totally lacking in the Do It gene.</i>
</blockquote>It’s so great to read narration like this, because Mia represents a larger population of teenage girls than she realizes; I found a lot of what she says relatable when I was growing up and I still feel that it’s applicable and valid now. I love that this book tackles such “taboo” topics, such as how to approach having The Talk with your significant other, literary merit, and other great social commentaries. There’s so much in this book that is important for young people—especially young girls, yes—to start thinking about. No, reading <i>Princess in Training</i> will not make a teenage girl an expert on comprehensive sex education—but it’s a GREAT start. We need more books out there like this one that are willing to talk about such a wide variety of topics from a realistic girl’s point of view, like Mia’s. <br /><br />I just like everything that this book has to offer and I adore it as the latter half of Mia’s journey begins. This is really the point when she starts to grow up a bit, shoulder some responsibilities, and, yes, bite the bullet and try to have The Talk with Michael Moscovitz, the love of her teenaged life. It’s witty and just the right amount of insane, but that doesn’t lessen its value—much like how Mia makes an argument for the relevance of pop culture references in academic work. Something can be hilarious and talk about things like Britney Spears and Sailor Moon without losing its meaning.<br /><br />I really love this book—I just thought I should reiterate that fact.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14449030653775592435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1404641027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1404641027" />
    <a title="Mehsi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6720768-mehsi"><img alt="Mehsi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588684075p2/6720768.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1404641027?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mehsi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mehsi" href="/user/show/6720768-mehsi">Mehsi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447287780" href="/book/show/26044736-royal-rebel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=for-girls-one-shelf">for-girls-one-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=warning-english-books">warning-english-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=away-laughing-on-a-fast-camel">away-laughing-on-a-fast-camel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=4-twinkling-stars">4-twinkling-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1404641027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1357481610213548199">This was a pretty great book in a (so far) shaping to be epic series.<br/><br/>Let me first start with the good things:<br/><br/>Mia is still awkward, but she does her best to fulfil her princess role, and you can see that she is getting better and better at it with each book. From a girl who didn’t want to be a princess, who refused to do princess stuff, she is now making decisions, helping out her people, and taking on her princess role. Of course, not always happily, but then again, I can understand that, you ha</span>
  <span id="freeText1357481610213548199" style="display:none">This was a pretty great book in a (so far) shaping to be epic series.<br /><br />Let me first start with the good things:<br /><br />Mia is still awkward, but she does her best to fulfil her princess role, and you can see that she is getting better and better at it with each book. From a girl who didn’t want to be a princess, who refused to do princess stuff, she is now making decisions, helping out her people, and taking on her princess role. Of course, not always happily, but then again, I can understand that, you have a great boyfriend, and then you are whisked away to your country again in the middle of summer break. I can just imagine that it must suck, you want a summer full of love, and instead you only get a bit of that and then you have to leave. Luckily we live in an era with phones and internet (hopefully Genovia does have that now).<br /><br />I also loved Mia’s attitude in the later parts of the books, especially with the whole president of school part. I just wanted to clap for her and encourage her to keep on going, that she could do this. The conclusion to the whole president chapter was great, though I do hope we don’t get a mega explosion between characters because of it. Then again, it is that character, so I guess we will be getting Michael Bay kind of explosions.<br /><br />I was also applauding for Meg Cabot not shying away from the sex topic. Oh no, don’t worry, it is all still very clean, nothing happens. But I am so happy to see that a book finally discusses this topic in the way this book did. It is not often, well, OK, I barely seen it, that a book writes about this topic so realistically. Generally characters just hop in the bed with characters without the Talk about if they both want it, if they both are ready for it, and if not, when they will be ready. Throughout the book we have Mia being totally stressed out, because she hears stuff (typical Mia, hears stuff and stresses out without checking facts). Though for once I could mostly sympathize with her (not all the way, because she made such a huge drama out of it). The talk and what comes out of that, it was great! I hope the other books will also still talk about this topic, and that we will see Mia’s and Michael’s relationship grow.<br /><br />Ah, yes, another good thing. Mia FINALLY didn’t let people run over her all the time. Still for a big part she did, but she finally put her foot down with a lot of Lilly stuff, and I was just so delighted to see her finally stand up for herself and what she wants.<br /><br />Now for the parts that weren’t really fun. Mia’s obsession with her baby brother. Dear Lord, girl are you the mother? I got SO sick of her meddling, acting like her mom is totally incompetent, and sure, the mom doesn’t always do things right, but she raised you, and you turned out right, so I think you don’t need to stalk your mom every x amount of time, or make her feel like she is a crap parent. I really wanted to just throw Mia out of window at times. Seriously, I do hope that the next book won’t have this obsession. Bah. Sisterly love is one thing, but this is just crazy.<br /><br />Lilly, once again I hated Lilly. Then again, with each passing book the hate grows. Lilly is the most annoying character (even more annoying than the grandmother) ever. Instead of getting better with each book she gets worse. Pushing people to do whatever she wants, calling her friend a name she doesn’t like and just don’t see that it might hurt her, acting a bitch when your friend is calling with her boyfriend, acting a bitch when people don’t instantly do your bidding. Then there is her fanatical ways. I don’t mind a character protesting against things, but Lilly? Lilly is taking it too far. She is the kind of person I would really avoid in real life.<br /><br />The English teacher. You see, that kind of teacher is a person who will ruin people’s talent and also the love for books or language. She is the kind of person I don’t like, people who push their likes and loves to someone, act like classics or high literature are so much better and then make bad remarks when someone says they prefer other stuff. Let people read and write whatever they want.<br />I am not saying that what Mia writes is always perfect, but to just cut of points because Mia uses pop-culture/modern references in her works? What the hell?<br /><br />What else? I think I have covered most of the topics that I wanted to discuss. I am quite excited to read the next book (hopefully it will be here soon).<br />Would I recommend this book? Yes, yes I would! Even with some bumps, it was still a great and funny read.<br /><br />Review first posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://twirlingbookprincess.com/">http://twirlingbookprincess.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1357481610213548199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText9681817922376229661" style="display:none">Again very similar to the others, especially in structure.<br>My only new comments to add are about Mia's speech at the end and Michael.<br><br>Me during Mia's speech:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420550290ra/13238276.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Me after Mia's speech:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438485569ra/15715434.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It was very inspiring but too long to cut and paste here. <span id="freeTextContainer15085980493456792349">See my entire binge read of this book and books 6-7 1/2 <a href='https://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2015/03/08/the-unofficial-princess-diaries-binge-review-where-jp-saves-the-series/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here.</a><br/><br/>Blah.<br/><br/>Besides, Princess in Waiting this is probably the most lackluster installment in the series. However, in retrospect I think Meg did an excellent job portraying a teenage girl. I hate to say it, when I was Mia’s age I probably acted a lot like her-though slightly less neurotic. And Teen Me is someone I really don’t want to be again.<br/><br/>That being said, I really wish there was more to this one. I could care less for either of the plots.</span>
  <span id="freeText15085980493456792349" style="display:none">See my entire binge read of this book and books 6-7 1/2 <a href="https://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2015/03/08/the-unofficial-princess-diaries-binge-review-where-jp-saves-the-series/" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br />Blah.<br /><br />Besides, Princess in Waiting this is probably the most lackluster installment in the series. However, in retrospect I think Meg did an excellent job portraying a teenage girl. I hate to say it, when I was Mia’s age I probably acted a lot like her-though slightly less neurotic. And Teen Me is someone I really don’t want to be again.<br /><br />That being said, I really wish there was more to this one. I could care less for either of the plots. The president plot I could care less for and in hindsight it really doesn’t add much to the series, save for being a plot point in the overall ridiculous plot that is seven.<br /><br />The sex plot….well, I might’ve cared for it more when I was fifteen.<br /><br />As a woman in her mid twenties though, I couldn’t help but roll my eyes at Mia’s obliviousness and freaking out.<br /><br />Again, very relevant to someone who is of that age group, but when you’re older you really could care less.<br /><br />There were some things that were enjoyable about this one that made it tolerable. The term Baby Licker was one of them. I also liked the fact that there seemed to be a heavy focus on friendship on this one.<br /><br />But sometimes, the friendships got immature. Like a certain scene at a slumber party when the characters discuss whether a new kid at school is a boy or girl.<br /><br />That just seemed a little rude.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<div id="review_52644945" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52644945" />
    <a title="Chelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1371249-chelle"><img alt="Chelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339623156p2/1371249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52644945?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelle" href="/user/show/1371249-chelle">Chelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer52644945&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52644945" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1461914988641641619">So I was ready to give up on Mia after Princess in Pink. All the prom freak outs made me think it was time to get back to adulthood. This one redeemed itself. Yes Mia still freaks out, it's who she is. She's 15, a sophomore in high school and thinks she's here to save the earth. She also has a boy friend who is a freshman in college and a very unusual life. I don't blame her for freaking out. <br/><br/>I enjoyed that she now has a teacher who will challenge her. Frankly if I had written like she writes in</span>
  <span id="freeText1461914988641641619" style="display:none">So I was ready to give up on Mia after Princess in Pink. All the prom freak outs made me think it was time to get back to adulthood. This one redeemed itself. Yes Mia still freaks out, it's who she is. She's 15, a sophomore in high school and thinks she's here to save the earth. She also has a boy friend who is a freshman in college and a very unusual life. I don't blame her for freaking out. <br /><br />I enjoyed that she now has a teacher who will challenge her. Frankly if I had written like she writes in high school I would have failed. Yes it's entertaining, but it's not scholarly. I really hope this drives Mia to do better. <br /><br />True to form Lilly decides to use Mia to further her own agenda. I hope Mia does not give up being student council president. She needs to stop letting herself be a pawn for her best friend and her grandmother. <br /><br />Yes all the "are we gonna do IT" talk is scary. The fact is she's too young to be having sex. It's also true that this is what girls are faced with today. They are pressured to have sex younger and younger, especially when they have older boyfriends. Sure Michael is a dreamboat and not like most guys his age, but he's still a freshman in college and in a totally different place in his life. Frankly I'm proud Mia stood up for herself and told him she wasn't ready. That Michael accepted that but also let her know his thoughts on the matter is refreshing. It's an example to other girls Mia's age that they don't have to have sex to have a boyfriend and should not be pressured into things they aren't ready for. It also gives them an example of how a boy should react to that assertion. That Michael says he won't wait forever, it's honest. Sure it seems like he's exerting pressure on Mia, but I think it's much more that he's just being open with her. They agreed on a timetable to revisit the issue which shows he's open to waiting a while, just not forever. <br /><br />All in all I can see Mia starting to really mature in this book which is making me want to finish the series. I want to see her settle into her own skin and take a freaking chill pill! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1461914988641641619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10777588280132633224">Best part of this book: When Mia looked up her mom's ex using Yahoo! People Search. I'm not sure I even remember that.<br/><br/>Most surprising part: How often Mia actually said "sex". This it the Doing It book and I just remembered everyone calling it that all the time. And they certainly do, but it's not as excessive as I remember.<br/><br/>Fun fact: When this book was originally released, it came out a lot earlier in England than in the US (if I remember correctly, it was a mistake somewhere).   <span id="freeText10777588280132633224" style="display:none">Best part of this book: When Mia looked up her mom's ex using Yahoo! People Search. I'm not sure I even remember that.<br /><br />Most surprising part: How often Mia actually said "sex". This it the Doing It book and I just remembered everyone calling it that all the time. And they certainly do, but it's not as excessive as I remember.<br /><br />Fun fact: When this book was originally released, it came out a lot earlier in England than in the US (if I remember correctly, it was a mistake somewhere). I was in college at the time and lent it to several friends.<br /><br />Actually, maybe the most surprising part is this is another one that worked a lot better for me these days. Mia is SO young and so obviously not ready for sex. And Michael's four years older and in college . . . it's a pretty realistic conflict and, this time through, Mia's reactions struck me as realistic, too.<br /><br />And, oh, I am loving Tina more than ever. She's such a good friend and has such a good head on her shoulders. Her advice to Mia is spot on.<br /><br />Also the presidential election! I forgot how great that is. Mia's really coming into her own.<br /><br />Another thing that struck me about these books is how well they integrate school. I mean, that's such a huge part of teen life and not necessarily a big part of YA. (Come to think of it, maybe some of the reason I'm feeling extra love for these books is that I haven't been loving most of the YA that's been published these days.)<br /><br />I'm mostly leaving these ratings at what I originally rated them, but this one is getting bumped from three to four.</span>

  <span id="freeText2659953299418836507" style="display:none">In this installment, Mia starts to realize her own abilities and begins to stand up for herself. Yes, she is still uncomfortable in her own skin, worries over everything and has the same streak of putting herself down, but she is beginning to grow up. And that is good.<br />One of the best things so far about this series is that Mia does grow and change while still retaining her lovely self-effacing personality. Her thoughts and ideas are becoming more adult. She's beginning to be a tiny bit more self-assured.<br />Mia has been in a relationship now for several months and the natural progression of that scares her. This are more mature themes to this one. Does she want to have sex and is she ready to do so? Can she have a conversation about this or just avoid the whole issue? And I really like where that goes. She stays true to herself and her feelings.<br />I really enjoy this series.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer7183879280489242769">Around page 50, Lana Weinberger, Mia's mortal enemy, teased her that soon her college-going boyfriend would expect her, as she <i>repeatedly</i> put it, to Do It with him. Thus began Mia's outlandish, childish, freakish and all other kinds of ish presumptions about Michael and his manly man needs. What even...<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440303000ra/15959204.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>A bunch of other stuff happened; Boris got hot over the summer, Mia won the Student Council Presidential Campaign, Lily turned into a complete nutter, Michael and Mia discussed Doing It, and other</span>
  <span id="freeText7183879280489242769" style="display:none">Around page 50, Lana Weinberger, Mia's mortal enemy, teased her that soon her college-going boyfriend would expect her, as she <i>repeatedly</i> put it, to Do It with him. Thus began Mia's outlandish, childish, freakish and all other kinds of ish presumptions about Michael and his manly man needs.     <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8263750-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587266605p2/8263750.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/8263750-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8263750-erin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8263750-erin?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8263750-erin?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2574276676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12072729314167094478">Mia is back at school and is now running for student body president after being nominated by Lily. So, on top of her princess training (and trying not to fail Geometry and figure out how to handle having Michael be at college), she has to figure out how to balance everything. <br/><br/>If there is one thing that I think I can say about Mia, it's that she's an accurate representation of teenage kids. Everything that happens to her is the worst thing that could happen, the end of the world. She thinks she'l</span>
  <span id="freeText12072729314167094478" style="display:none">Mia is back at school and is now running for student body president after being nominated by Lily. So, on top of her princess training (and trying not to fail Geometry and figure out how to handle having Michael be at college), she has to figure out how to balance everything. <br /><br />If there is one thing that I think I can say about Mia, it's that she's an accurate representation of teenage kids. Everything that happens to her is the worst thing that could happen, the end of the world. She thinks she'll never be able to get over anything and overthinks everything. But, while I do feel like it's accurate (from what I can remember) it's incredibly annoying to read. I keep thinking that everything will calm down a bit and she'll think a little bit more rationally, but it never seems to happen. <br /><br />I'm not sure if Mia has really developed at all so far in this series. She seems to still be the same girl who we saw in book one despite this now being on book six. <br /><br />Throughout this one, she dotes on her baby brother to incredible extremes. It got to the point where I wondered if she thought that her mother should even be raising him. Mia had so little faith in her mother that it was baffling. Does she think she really turned out that bad? <br /><br />After listening to what Lana told her (which you would think she would know better than to do that), the book tailspins into Mia consistently worrying about her relationship with Michael and instead of talking to him about it she just worries more and more. I know talking can be difficult, but I hate how the romance in this book was all driven by Mia worrying about something that could have been taken care of quickly if she would have talked to him sooner rather than later about it. <br /><br />I think I've said this before, but I think I'm going to stop here. The lack of character development and the constant whining about everything is more than I can bear. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12072729314167094478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11831059550927682236">3.5 stars. I continue to not like Lily because she does things without asking anybody. She nominates Mia for class president without asking. And she's really doing this so SHE can be president. That's not how things work. Mia agonizes about boys and sex and is so immature about it sometimes. I should have counted the number of times she said 'doing it' because it got old really fast. But still, I am hooked on the story as a whole and will keep going!</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_214734698" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/214734698" />
    <a title="hpboy13" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6427364-hpboy13"><img alt="hpboy13" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395922187p2/6427364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/214734698?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="hpboy13" class="user" itemprop="url" name="hpboy13" href="/user/show/6427364-hpboy13">hpboy13</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6427364-hpboy13?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6427364-hpboy13?shelf=best-of-ya">best-of-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer214734698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1531474920293756887">Absolutely hilarious, and a sheer joy to read! Here, we finally see Mia maturing into the princess she will one day become.<br/><br/>ETA 10 years later: To my surprise, PIT held up better than expected, given that it’s between two of the weaker installments in the series. But as we enter the back half of the series, and finally move on from Mia’s freshman year, and this is really the book where Mia begins to grow into a leader. It’s very enjoyable to read about, because after five books of Mia running aro</span>
  <span id="freeText1531474920293756887" style="display:none">Absolutely hilarious, and a sheer joy to read! Here, we finally see Mia maturing into the princess she will one day become.<br /><br />ETA 10 years later: To my surprise, PIT held up better than expected, given that it’s between two of the weaker installments in the series. But as we enter the back half of the series, and finally move on from Mia’s freshman year, and this is really the book where Mia begins to grow into a leader. It’s very enjoyable to read about, because after five books of Mia running around like a chicken sans head, here she finally takes charge and makes things happen – and honestly, she’s a rather remarkable teen, one who evidently will make a great leader. Just look at how she stands up for underdogs and includes them in her social circle – something she never would have done a few months earlier.<br /><br />In fact, the entire gang does some growing up here. I especially enjoyed the fact that Boris got hot, and that Grandmere is now an accepted (though occasionally misguided) ally to Mia. This book is also Lana’s last stand as the chief antagonist, as the next book introduces a new one. And honestly, Lana made for a very good villain, and her takedown was supremely enjoyable to read. And I applaud Cabot for moving on, because Mia has started to outgrow Lana as a villain.<br /><br />The inclusion of Ms. Martinez as a thinly veiled jab at all of Cabot’s critics (who deride the book series for relying too much on pop culture) actually works really well, especially because it’s a very realistic turn for Mia: even if she has a talent, the appreciation of said talent is rarely unanimous. I also don’t mind because I very much come down on the side of Mia – nothing wrong with pop culture references (even if I think Buzzfeed-y lists of movies are a bit much to include in a book).<br /><br />Honestly, by far the weakest point of this book was the plot about Mia’s fear of Doing It with Michael. I get what Cabot’s issue is here: like many TV shows that get the main couple together early in the run, there’s a struggle to find conflict for the couple to keep it interesting. And to be fair, the plot about a couple having issues with Doing It is far less contrived than last book’s prom debacle. But it’s just not very interesting to read about Mia agonizing over something that would be (and usually is) resolved with a simple conversation.<br /><br />On the whole, this book series remains as fluffy, sweet, and hilarious as I remember it – and it’s a lot of fun to reread!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1531474920293756887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3007514368" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3007514368" />
    <a title="Reading Relish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61495116-reading-relish"><img alt="Reading Relish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597187862p2/61495116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3007514368?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Relish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Relish" href="/user/show/61495116-reading-relish">Reading Relish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330420389" href="/book/show/93746.Sixsational">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=school">school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=royalty">royalty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61495116-reading-relish?shelf=diaries">diaries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3007514368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3915073943235618941">I know some people find Mia’s constant overthinking as annoying, but think about it:<br/><br/>•She’s being trained to become a princess, a title she never asked for.<br/><br/>•Even with a princess title, she’s still treated as an outcast at school.<br/><br/>•Now that she has a boyfriend, Mia feels pressured to be perfect. Even though MICHAEL doesn’t expect her to be perfect, she still feels pressured by others (including Lana and her friends) to be and act a certain way.<br/><br/>•Her mom just had a baby, and the father is Mia’s forme</span>
  <span id="freeText3915073943235618941" style="display:none">I know some people find Mia’s constant overthinking as annoying, but think about it:<br /><br />•She’s being trained to become a princess, a title she never asked for.<br /><br />•Even with a princess title, she’s still treated as an outcast at school.<br /><br />•Now that she has a boyfriend, Mia feels pressured to be perfect. Even though MICHAEL doesn’t expect her to be perfect, she still feels pressured by others (including Lana and her friends) to be and act a certain way.<br /><br />•Her mom just had a baby, and the father is Mia’s former math teacher. Enough said there.<br /><br />For these reasons, I totally get why Mia is stressed out all the time. Because of that, I want what’s best for her. With everything she’s doing through, she honestly deserves a break.<br /><br />Even with Mia being stressed out, these books continue to make me smile! Whether it’s Mia finding herself in a hilarious situation, or her finding the courage to face some kind of fear, I constantly find myself turning the next page.<br /><br />I gotta say, Mia NAILED IT with that speech! I was cheering her on the whole time! And Lana’s reaction was PRICELESS! There’s no way Mia’s going to back out now!<br /><br />Also, the references to the Disney movie adaptations were hilarious! I wish Rick Riordan would roast the Percy Jackson movie adaptation the way Meg Cabot does with The Princess Diaries movies!<br /><br />Are these the best book I’ve EVER read? No. But the Princess Diaries books are perfect when you need something light and fluffy.<br /><br />I’m determined to finish The Princess Diaries series in 2020, or at least the main novels, if I can’t get to all the novellas. I’m halfway now!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3915073943235618941" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RIS6Xy59Jn/ZC1Lx3TEzmNVIZ/fsSNtYIAYC7/t23e4iVndBj8IfHVFR5JNmTL35aKwCAdZE1d+GiUGpR3eHcw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9799dLpGNzBVGTECamTlkClr+0m3qlH9qhAW/p0iv4ORbbBqG/kOUt1Dh2DRGWvxlI+ev42mX3oMn1W4ISPlHg==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16234685295374730786">Librarian note: AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll' title='Jenny Carroll' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot' title='Patricia Cabot' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br/><br/>Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flun</span>
  <span id="freeText16234685295374730786" style="display:none">Librarian note: AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll" title="Jenny Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot" title="Patricia Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br /><br />Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flunked freshman Algebra twice, then decided to cut her own bangs. After six years as an undergrad at Indiana University, Meg moved to New York City (in the middle of a sanitation worker strike) to pursue a career as an illustrator, at which she failed miserably, forcing her to turn to her favorite hobby--writing novels--for emotional succor. She worked various jobs to pay the rent, including a decade-long stint as the assistant manager of a 700 bed freshmen dormitory at NYU, a position she still occasionally misses. <br /><br />She is now the author of nearly fifty books for both adults and teens, selling fifteen million copies worldwide, many of which have been #1 New York Times bestsellers, most notably The Princess Diaries series, which is currently being published in over 38 countries, and was made into two hit movies by Disney. In addition, Meg wrote the Mediator and 1-800-Where-R-You? series (on which the television series, Missing, was based), two All-American Girl books, Teen Idol, Avalon High, How to Be Popular, Pants on Fire, Jinx, a series of novels written entirely in email format (Boy Next Door, Boy Meets Girl, and Every Boy's Got One), a mystery series (Size 12 Is Not Fat/ Size 14 Is Not Fat Either/Big Boned), and a chick-lit series called Queen of Babble. <br /><br />Meg is now writing a new children's series called Allie Finkle's Rules for Girls. Her new paranormal series, Abandon, debuts in Summer of 2011. <br /><br />Meg currently divides her time between Key West, Indiana, and New York City with a primary cat (one-eyed Henrietta), various back-up cats, and her husband, who doesn't know he married a fire horse. Please don't tell him. <br /><br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/45023-airhead" rel="nofollow noopener">Airhead</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43768-the-princess-diaries" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Diaries</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41667-mediator" rel="nofollow noopener">Mediator</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16234685295374730786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>

      </div>

    </div>
